3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes CNI Network Plugin Interface Architecture

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the CNI (Container Network Interface) integration: the CNI plugin invocation, the network namespace setup, the IP address management (IPAM) call, and the network plugin manager that coordinates CNI calls during pod creation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

  ],

  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of the findings:

## CNI Network Plugin Integration in Kubernetes v1.32

In Kubernetes v1.32, the kubelet no longer invokes CNI plugins directly (that changed with the dockershim removal in v1.24). Instead it orchestrates through the CRI layer. The key files are:

### CNI Plugin Invocation
- **`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go`** — `createPodSandbox()` is the core invocation path; it calls `RunPodSandbox` via CRI which triggers the container runtime (containerd/CRI-O) to invoke CNI plugins
- **`staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go`** — CRI client: `RunPodSandbox()` and `UpdateRuntimeConfig()` send the gRPC requests to the runtime

### Network Namespace Setup
- **`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go`** — `NetworkNamespaceForPod()`, `NamespacesForPod()`, `PodSandboxChanged()` configure whether a pod gets its own network namespace or shares the host's
- **`pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network_linux.go`** — Linux iptables rules initialized alongside pod networking

### IPAM (IP Address Management)
- **`pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go`** — `updatePodCIDR()` propagates pod CIDRs down to the runtime (comment: "kubelet → generic runtime → runtime shim → network plugin")
- **`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`** — `UpdatePodCIDR()` sends CIDR to `UpdateRuntimeConfig` for the CNI IPAM plugin
- **`pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go`**, **`ipam/cidr_allocator.go`**, **`ipam/range_allocator.go`** — Node-level IPAM that partitions cluster CIDR into per-node ranges

### Network Plugin Manager
- **`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`** — `kubeGenericRuntimeManager` is the network plugin manager; `SyncPod()` coordinates CNI calls during pod creation
- **`pk

Since the dockershim was removed in v1.24, the kubelet no longer invokes CNI plugins directly; instead it delegates network setup to the container runtime (containerd, CRI-O) via the Container Runtime Interface (CRI). Here is a breakdown of the relevant source files:\\n\\n**CNI Plugin Invocation (via CRI):**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go`: The `createPodSandbox()` function is the core CNI invocation path. It calls `m.runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` which triggers the container runtime to invoke the CNI plugin chain. `generatePodSandboxConfig()` and `generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` prepare the pod sandbox configuration including port mappings and namespace options that the container runtime uses when calling CNI.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go`: Implements the CRI client. `RunPodSandbox()` sends the gRPC request to the container runtime which then invokes CNI plugins. `UpdateRuntimeConfig()` propagates the pod CIDR to the runtime's network plugin (comment: 'This translates to an Event notification to the network plugin').\\n\\n**Network Namespace Setup:**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go`: `NetworkNamespaceForPod()` determines whether a pod gets its own network namespace (POD mode) or shares the host network namespace (NODE mode). `NamespacesForPod()` constructs the full NamespaceOption including network namespace settings. `PodSandboxChanged()` detects if the network namespace mode changed, triggering sandbox recreation with new CNI setup.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox_linux.go`: Linux-specific sandbox resource configuration.\\n\\n**IPAM (IP Address Management):**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go`: `updatePodCIDR()` propagates the pod CIDR to the container runtime. The comment on line 54 explicitly states the path: 'kubelet -> generic runtime -> runtime shim -> network plugin'. This CIDR is used by the CNI IPAM plugin.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`: `UpdatePodCIDR()` calls `m.runtimeService.UpdateRuntimeConfig()` with the pod CIDR in a `NetworkConfig`, passing it down to the container runtime's network plugin for IPAM.\\n- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go`: Node IPAM controller that assigns pod CIDRs (podCIDRs) to Nodes - this is the cluster-level IPAM that assigns IP ranges per node.\\n- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidr_allocator.go`: Defines the `CIDRAllocator` interface and allocator types (RangeAllocator, CloudAllocator, IPAMFromCluster, IPAMFromCloud).\\n- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/range_allocator.go`: Range-based CIDR allocator that allocates pod CIDRs to nodes from the cluster CIDR range.\\n\\n**Network Plugin Manager (coordinates CNI calls):**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`: `kubeGenericRuntimeManager` is the network plugin manager. Its `SyncPod()` function coordinates CNI calls during pod creation (calling `createPodSandbox()` which triggers CNI) and tracks the results with `SetupNetwork`/`TeardownNetwork` SyncActions.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go`: Defines the `Runtime` interface including `UpdatePodCIDR()` method signature.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/sync_result.go`: Defines `SetupNetwork` and `TeardownNetwork` `SyncAction` constants used to track network setup/teardown as part of pod lifecycle operations.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network_linux.go`: Linux-specific kubelet network initialization including iptables rules needed for pod networking.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_node_status.go`: Reads `node.Spec.PodCIDRs` and calls `updatePodCIDR()` to propagate to the runtime/CNI plugin.\"\n}\n",

Since dockershim was removed in v1.24, the kubelet no longer invokes CNI plugins directly; instead it delegates network setup to the container runtime (containerd, CRI-O) via the Container Runtime Interface (CRI). Here is a breakdown of the relevant source files:\\n\\n**CNI Plugin Invocation (via CRI):**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go`: The `createPodSandbox()` function is the core CNI invocation path. It calls `m.runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()` which triggers the container runtime to invoke the CNI plugin chain. `generatePodSandboxConfig()` and `generatePodSandboxLinuxConfig()` prepare the pod sandbox configuration including port mappings and namespace options that the container runtime uses when calling CNI.\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go`: Implements the CRI client. `RunPodSandbox()` sends the gRPC request to the container runtime which then invokes CNI plugins. `UpdateRuntimeConfig()` propagates the pod CIDR to the runtime's network plugin (the comment says: 'This translates to an Event notification to the network plugin').\\n\\n**Network Namespace Setup:**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/util/util.go`: `NetworkNamespaceForPod()` determines whether a pod gets its own network namespace (POD mode) or shares the host network namespace (NODE mode). `NamespacesForPod()` constructs the full NamespaceOption including network namespace settings passed to the container runtime. `PodSandboxChanged()` detects if the network namespace mode changed, triggering sandbox recreation and new CNI calls.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network_linux.go`: Linux-specific kubelet network initialization including iptables rules (KUBE-IPTABLES-HINT, KUBE-FIREWALL) needed alongside pod networking.\\n\\n**IPAM (IP Address Management):**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_network.go`: `updatePodCIDR()` propagates the pod CIDR to the container runtime. The comment explicitly states the path: 'kubelet -> generic runtime -> runtime shim -> network plugin'. This CIDR is consumed by the CNI IPAM plugin (e.g., host-local) in the container runtime.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`: `UpdatePodCIDR()` calls `m.runtimeService.UpdateRuntimeConfig()` with the pod CIDR in a `NetworkConfig`, passing it to the container runtime's network plugin for IPAM configuration.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kubelet_node_status.go`: Reads `node.Spec.PodCIDRs` from node status and calls `updatePodCIDR()` to propagate down to CNI.\\n- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go`: Node IPAM controller (`NewNodeIpamController`) that assigns pod CIDRs to Nodes - this is the cluster-level IPAM that partitions the cluster CIDR into per-node ranges used by CNI IPAM plugins.\\n- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/cidr_allocator.go`: Defines the `CIDRAllocator` interface and allocator types (RangeAllocator, CloudAllocator, IPAMFromCluster, IPAMFromCloud).\\n- `pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/range_allocator.go`: Range-based CIDR allocator that allocates pod CIDRs to nodes from the cluster CIDR range.\\n\\n**Network Plugin Manager (coordinates CNI calls during pod creation):**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`: `kubeGenericRuntimeManager` acts as the network plugin manager. Its `SyncPod()` function coordinates CNI calls during pod creation by calling `createPodSandbox()` which triggers CNI. Comments at line 1224 explicitly mention 'createPodSandbox can return an error from CNI'. `UpdatePodCIDR()` sends CIDR updates to the container runtime's CNI configuration.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go`: Defines the `Runtime` interface including the `UpdatePodCIDR()` method, establishing the contract between kubelet and the network plugin manager.\\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/sync_result.go`: Defines `SetupNetwork` and `TeardownNetwork` `SyncAction` constants for tracking network setup/teardown in pod lifecycle operations (`SyncPod` and `KillPod`).\"\n}\n",
